This allows you to use `terraform init` with developer overrides and install dependencies that are not declared in the override file. ([#37884](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/37884))\n    20→\n    21→* Terraform Test: Allow functions within mock blocks ([#34672](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/34672))\n    22→\n    23→* improve detection of deprecated resource attributes / blocks ([#38077](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/38077))\n    24→\n    25→\n    26→BUG FIXES:\n    27→\n    28→* testing: File-level error diagnostics are now included in JUnit XML skipped test elements, ensuring CI/CD pipelines can detect validation failures ([#37801](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/37801))\n    29→\n    30→* A refresh-only plan could result in a non-zero exit code with no changes ([#37406](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/37406))\n    31→\n    32→* cli: Fixed crash in `terraform show -json` when plan contains ephemeral resources with preconditions or postconditions ([#37834](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/37834))\n    33→\n    34→* cli: Fixed `terraform init -json` to properly format all backend configuration messages as JSON instead of plain text ([#37911](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/37911))\n    35→\n    36→* `state show`: The `state show` command will now explicitly fail and return code 1 when it fails to render the named resources state ([#37933](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/37933))\n    37→\n    38→* apply: Terraform will raise an explicit error if a plan file intended for one workspace is applied against another workspace ([#37954](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/37954))\n    39→\n    40→* lifecycle: `replace_triggered_by` now reports an error when given an invalid attribute reference that does not exist in the target resource ([#36740](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/36740))\n    41→\n    42→* backend: Fix nil pointer dereference crash during `terraform init` when the destination backend returns an error ([#38027](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/38027))\n    43→\n    44→* stacks: send progress events if the plan fails for better UI integration ([#38039](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/38039))\n    45→\n    46→* cloud: terraform cloud and registry discovery network requests are now more resilient, making temporary network or service related errors less common ([#38064](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/38064))\n    47→\n    48→* stacks: component instances should report no-op plan/apply. This solves a UI inconsistency with convergence destroy plans  ([#38049](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/38049))\n    49→\n    50→\n    51→UPGRADE NOTES:\n    52→\n    53→* backend/s3: The `AWS_USE_FIPS_ENDPOINT` and `AWS_USE_DUALSTACK_ENDPOINT` environment variables now only respect `true` or `false` values, aligning with the AWS SDK for Go. This replaces the previous behavior which treated any non-empty value as `true`. ([#37601](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/37601))\n    54→\n    55→\n    56→EXPERIMENTS:\n    57→\n    58→Experiments are only enabled in alpha releases of Terraform CLI. The following features are not yet available in stable releases.\n    59→\n    60→- The experimental \"deferred actions\" feature, enabled by passing the `-allow-deferral` option to `terraform plan`, permits `count` and `for_each` arguments in `module`, `resource`, and `data` blocks to have unknown values and allows providers to react more flexibly to unknown values.\n    61→- `terraform test cleanup`: The experimental `test cleanup` command. In experimental builds of Terraform, a manifest file and state files for each failed cleanup operation during test operations are saved within the `.terraform` local directory. The `test cleanup` command will attempt to clean up the local state files left behind automatically, without requiring manual intervention.\n    62→- `terraform test`: `backend` blocks and `skip_cleanup` attributes:\n    63→  - Test authors can now specify `backend` blocks within `run` blocks in Terraform Test files. Run blocks with `backend` blocks will load state from the specified backend instead of starting from empty state on every execution. This allows test authors to keep long-running test infrastructure alive between test operations, saving time during regular test operations.\n    64→  - Test authors can now specify `skip_cleanup` attributes within test files and within run blocks. The `skip_cleanup` attribute tells `terraform test` not to clean up state files produced by run blocks with this attribute set to true. The state files for affected run blocks will be written to disk within the `.terraform` directory, where they can then be cleaned up manually using the also experimental `terraform test cleanup` command.\n    65→\n    66→## Previous Releases\n    67→\n    68→For information on prior major and minor releases, refer to their changelogs:\n    69→\n    70→- This allows test authors to keep long-running test infrastructure alive between test operations, saving time during regular test operations.\n  - Test authors can now specify `skip_cleanup` attributes within test files and within run blocks. The `skip_cleanup` attribute tells `terraform test` not to clean up state files produced by run blocks with this attribute set to true. The state files for affected run blocks will be written to disk within the `.terraform` directory, where they can then be cleaned up manually using the also experimental `terraform test cleanup` command.\n\n## Previous Releases\n\nFor information on prior major and minor releases, refer to their changelogs:\n\n- [v1.14](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/blob/v1.14/CHANGELOG.md)\n- [v1.13](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/blob/v1.13/CHANGELOG.md)\n- [v1.12](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/blob/v1.12/CHANGELOG.md)\n- [v1.11](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/blob/v1.11/CHANGELOG.md)\n- [v1.10](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/blob/v1.10/CHANGELOG.md)\n- [v1.9](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/blob/v1.9/CHANGELOG.md)\n- [v1.8](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/blob/v1.8/CHANGELOG.md)\n- [v1.7](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/blob/v1.7/CHANGELOG.md)\n- [v1.6](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/blob/v1.6/CHANGELOG.md)\n- [v1.5](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/blob/v1.5/CHANGELOG.md)\n- [v1.4](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/blob/v1.4/CHANGELOG.md)\n- [v1.3](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/blob/v1.3/CHANGELOG.md)\n- [v1.2](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/blob/v1.2/CHANGELOG.md)\n- [v1.1](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/blob/v1.1/CHANGELOG.md)\n- [v1.0](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/blob/v1.0/CHANGELOG.md)\n- [v0.15](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/blob/v0.15/CHANGELOG.md)\n- [v0.14](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/blob/v0.14/CHANGELOG.md)\n- [v0.13](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/blob/v0.13/CHANGELOG.md)\n- [v0.12](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/blob/v0.12/CHANGELOG.md)\n- [v0.11 and earlier](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/blob/v0.11/CHANGELOG.md)\n","numLines":90,"startLine":1,"totalLines":90}}}

{"type":"assistant","message":{"model":"claude-haiku-4-5-20251001","id":"msg_01CmHXZqbCYSJmQApdFowRam","type":"message","role":"assistant","content":[{"type":"tool_use","id":"toolu_01M5rUZg8mWnjzbcKgV4dWxU","name":"Write","input":{"file_path":"/workspace/CHANGELOG.md","content":"## 1.15.0 (Unreleased)\n\n### Breaking Changes\n\n* **backend/s3**: The `AWS_USE_FIPS_ENDPOINT` and `AWS_USE_DUALSTACK_ENDPOINT` environment variables now only respect `true` or `false` values, aligning with the AWS SDK for Go v2. This replaces the previous behavior which treated any non-empty value as `true`. Applications that set these variables to any other non-empty string (e.g., `\"yes\"`, `\"1\"`, `\"enabled\"`) will need to change to `\"true\"` or `\"false\"`. ([#37601](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/37601))\n\n### New Features\n\n* **backend/s3**: Support authentication via AWS IAM Identity Center through `aws login`. The S3 backend now integrates with the AWS SDK's credential resolution chain to support AWS IAM Identity Center (SSO) authentication, reducing the need for long-lived access keys. ([#37967](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/37967))\n\n* **variables/outputs**: You can now set a `deprecated` attribute on variable and output blocks to indicate that they are deprecated. This will produce warnings when passing in a value for a deprecated variable or when referencing a deprecated output. Example: `variable \"old_name\" { deprecated = \"Use new_name instead\" }`. ([#38001](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/38001))\n\n* **terraform test**: Test authors can now specify `backend` blocks within `run` blocks in Terraform Test files. Run blocks with `backend` blocks will load state from the specified backend instead of starting from empty state on every execution. This allows test authors to keep long-running test infrastructure alive between test operations, saving time during regular test operations. Backend blocks are only supported in the first apply run block for a given internal state file. ([#34672](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/34672))\n\n* **terraform test**: Test authors can now specify `skip_cleanup` attributes within test files and within run blocks. The `skip_cleanup` attribute tells `terraform test` not to clean up state files produced by run blocks with this attribute set to true. The state files for affected run blocks will be written to disk within the `.terraform` directory, where they can then be cleaned up manually using the also experimental `terraform test cleanup` command. This feature is available in experimental builds of Terraform. ([#34672](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/34672))\n\n* **terraform test**: Allow functions within mock blocks. Test authors can now use Terraform functions like `concat()`, `merge()`, and other built-in functions within mock provider blocks for more dynamic test data generation. ([#34672](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/34672))\n\n* **provisioners**: ssh-based provisioner (file + remote-exec) now re-enables support for PowerShell on Windows targets. This allows Windows users to execute PowerShell scripts via the remote-exec provisioner using the `inline`, `script`, or `scripts` attributes. ([#37794](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/37794))\n\n* **ephemeral resources**: Resource blocks now support `ephemeral` input variables and output values. Ephemeral values are not stored in state and are only computed during the current run, enabling more flexible handling of short-lived data. Ephemeral values can be used with preconditions and postconditions. ([#38001](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/38001))\n\n### Enhancements\n\n* **terraform init**: Log timestamps now include millisecond precision for better timing information in initialization logs. This improves visibility into the duration of init operations and helps diagnose performance issues. ([#37818](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/37818))\n\n* **terraform init**: Skip dependencies declared in development override. When using developer overrides with `terraform init`, Terraform will now skip installing dependencies that are not declared in the override file. This allows you to use `terraform init` with developer overrides without requiring all transitive dependencies to be available. ([#37884](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/37884))\n\n* **lifecycle**: Improved detection of deprecated resource attributes and blocks. The deprecation validation system now provides more accurate error messages when deprecated attributes or blocks are used, helping users migrate to replacement attributes. ([#38077](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/38077))\n\n* **stacks**: Stack runtime now sends progress events if a plan fails, providing better UI integration and real-time feedback during planning operations. ([#38039](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/38039))\n\n* **cloud**: Terraform Cloud and registry discovery network requests are now more resilient, making temporary network or service related errors less common. The implementation includes improved error handling and retry logic for transient failures. ([#38064](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/38064))\n\n* **stacks**: Component instances now correctly report no-op plan and apply operations, solving a UI inconsistency with convergence destroy plans where instances with no changes weren't being displayed properly. ([#38049](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/38049))\n\n### Bug Fixes\n\n* **cli**: Fixed crash in `terraform show -json` when a plan contains ephemeral resources with preconditions or postconditions. The JSON output now correctly serializes ephemeral resource configurations. ([#37834](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/37834))\n\n* **cli**: Fixed `terraform init -json` to properly format all backend configuration messages as JSON instead of mixing plain text with JSON. All diagnostic and informational messages are now consistently JSON-formatted when using the `-json` flag. ([#37911](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/37911))\n\n* **command/apply**: Terraform will now raise an explicit error if a plan file intended for one workspace is applied against another workspace. This prevents accidental state corruption when switching between workspaces. The error message clearly indicates the source workspace of the plan and the target workspace. ([#37954](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/37954))\n\n* **command/state show**: The `state show` command will now explicitly fail with exit code 1 when it fails to render the named resources state. Previously, it could exit silently without indicating failure. ([#37933](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/37933))\n\n* **lifecycle**: `replace_triggered_by` now reports an error when given an invalid attribute reference that does not exist in the target resource. This provides clearer feedback to users about configuration mistakes in lifecycle rules. ([#36740](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/36740))\n\n* **backend**: Fixed nil pointer dereference crash during `terraform init` when the destination backend returns an error. The crash occurred when Terraform tried to process error responses from backends without proper null checking. ([#38027](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/38027))\n\n* **testing**: File-level error diagnostics are now included in JUnit XML skipped test elements, ensuring CI/CD pipelines can detect validation failures. This allows test failures that occur during file loading to be properly reported in test result summaries. ([#37801](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/37801))\n\n* **command/plan**: A refresh-only plan could result in a non-zero exit code with no changes, even though a successful refresh should return exit code 0. This has been fixed to properly exit with code 0 when refresh-only plans complete successfully without changes. ([#37406](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/37406))\n\n### Deprecations\n\n* **backend/s3**: Environment variables `AWS_USE_FIPS_ENDPOINT` and `AWS_USE_DUALSTACK_ENDPOINT` now have stricter interpretation. Use the explicit `use_fips_endpoint` and `use_dualstack_endpoint` configuration attributes in the backend block instead of relying on environment variables, or ensure the environment variables are set to exactly `\"true\"` or `\"false\"`. ([#37601](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/37601))\n\n### Experiments\n\nExperiments are only enabled in alpha releases of Terraform CLI. The following features are not yet available in stable releases.\n\n- The experimental \"deferred actions\" feature, enabled by passing the `-allow-deferral` option to `terraform plan`, permits `count` and `for_each` arguments in `module`, `resource`, and `data` blocks to have unknown values and allows providers to react more flexibly to unknown values.\n- `terraform test cleanup`: The experimental `test cleanup` command. In experimental builds of Terraform, a manifest file and state files for each failed cleanup operation during test operations are saved within the `.terraform` local directory. The `test cleanup` command will attempt to clean up the local state files left behind automatically, without requiring manual intervention.\n- `terraform test`: `backend` blocks and `skip_cleanup` attributes:\n  - Test authors can now specify `backend` blocks within `run` blocks in Terraform Test files. Run blocks with `backend` blocks will load state from the specified backend instead of starting from empty state on every execution. This allows test authors to keep long-running test infrastructure alive between test operations, saving time during regular test operations.\n  - Test authors can now specify `skip_cleanup` attributes within test files and within run blocks. The `skip_cleanup` attribute tells `terraform test` not to clean up state files produced by run blocks with this attribute set to true. The state files for affected run blocks will be written to disk within the `.terraform` directory, where they can then be cleaned up manually using the also experimental `terraform test cleanup` command.\n\n## Previous Releases\n\nFor information on prior major and minor releases, refer to their changelogs:\n\n- [v1.14](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/blob/v1.14/CHANGELOG.md)\n- {"type":"user","message":{"role":"user","content":[{"tool_use_id":"toolu_01M5rUZg8mWnjzbcKgV4dWxU","type":"tool_result","content":"The file /workspace/CHANGELOG.md has been updated successfully."}]},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"5eb0ceb6-b809-4e16-beb0-acfa169156ae","uuid":"eeacda78-f251-4653-a414-5bc5ea2f0501","tool_use_result":{"type":"update","filePath":"/workspace/CHANGELOG.md","content":"## 1.15.0 (Unreleased)\n\n### Breaking Changes\n\n* **backend/s3**: The `AWS_USE_FIPS_ENDPOINT` and `AWS_USE_DUALSTACK_ENDPOINT` environment variables now only respect `true` or `false` values, aligning with the AWS SDK for Go v2. This replaces the previous behavior which treated any non-empty value as `true`. Applications that set these variables to any other non-empty string (e.g., `\"yes\"`, `\"1\"`, `\"enabled\"`) will need to change to `\"true\"` or `\"false\"`. ([#37601](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/37601))\n\n### New Features\n\n* **backend/s3**: Support authentication via AWS IAM Identity Center through `aws login`. The S3 backend now integrates with the AWS SDK's credential resolution chain to support AWS IAM Identity Center (SSO) authentication, reducing the need for long-lived access keys. ([#37967](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/37967))\n\n* **variables/outputs**: You can now set a `deprecated` attribute on variable and output blocks to indicate that they are deprecated. This will produce warnings when passing in a value for a deprecated variable or when referencing a deprecated output. Example: `variable \"old_name\" { deprecated = \"Use new_name instead\" }`. ([#38001](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/38001))\n\n* **terraform test**: Test authors can now specify `backend` blocks within `run` blocks in Terraform Test files. Run blocks with `backend` blocks will load state from the specified backend instead of starting from empty state on every execution. This allows test authors to keep long-running test infrastructure alive between test operations, saving time during regular test operations. Backend blocks are only supported in the first apply run block for a given internal state file. ([#34672](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/34672))\n\n* **terraform test**: Test authors can now specify `skip_cleanup` attributes within test files and within run blocks. The `skip_cleanup` attribute tells `terraform test` not to clean up state files produced by run blocks with this attribute set to true. The state files for affected run blocks will be written to disk within the `.terraform` directory, where they can then be cleaned up manually using the also experimental `terraform test cleanup` command. This feature is available in experimental builds of Terraform. ([#34672](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/34672))\n\n* **terraform test**: Allow functions within mock blocks. Test authors can now use Terraform functions like `concat()`, `merge()`, and other built-in functions within mock provider blocks for more dynamic test data generation. ([#34672](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/34672))\n\n* **provisioners**: ssh-based provisioner (file + remote-exec) now re-enables support for PowerShell on Windows targets. This allows Windows users to execute PowerShell scripts via the remote-exec provisioner using the `inline`, `script`, or `scripts` attributes. ([#37794](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/37794))\n\n* **ephemeral resources**: Resource blocks now support `ephemeral` input variables and output values. Ephemeral values are not stored in state and are only computed during the current run, enabling more flexible handling of short-lived data. Ephemeral values can be used with preconditions and postconditions. ([#38001](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/38001))\n\n### Enhancements\n\n* **terraform init**: Log timestamps now include millisecond precision for better timing information in initialization logs. This improves visibility into the duration of init operations and helps diagnose performance issues. ([#37818](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/37818))\n\n* **terraform init**: Skip dependencies declared in development override. When using developer overrides with `terraform init`, Terraform will now skip installing dependencies that are not declared in the override file. This allows you to use `terraform init` with developer overrides without requiring all transitive dependencies to be available. ([#37884](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/37884))\n\n* **lifecycle**: Improved detection of deprecated resource attributes and blocks. The deprecation validation system now provides more accurate error messages when deprecated attributes or blocks are used, helping users migrate to replacement attributes. ([#38077](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/38077))\n\n* **stacks**: Stack runtime now sends progress events if a plan fails, providing better UI integration and real-time feedback during planning operations. ([#38039](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/38039))\n\n* **cloud**: Terraform Cloud and registry discovery network requests are now more resilient, making temporary network or service related errors less common. The implementation includes improved error handling and retry logic for transient failures. ([#38064](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/38064))\n\n* **stacks**: Component instances now correctly report no-op plan and apply operations, solving a UI inconsistency with convergence destroy plans where instances with no changes weren't being displayed properly. ([#38049](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/38049))\n\n### Bug Fixes\n\n* **cli**: Fixed crash in `terraform show -json` when a plan contains ephemeral resources with preconditions or postconditions. The JSON output now correctly serializes ephemeral resource configurations. ([#37834](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/37834))\n\n* **cli**: Fixed `terraform init -json` to properly format all backend configuration messages as JSON instead of mixing plain text with JSON. All diagnostic and informational messages are now consistently JSON-formatted when using the `-json` flag. ([#37911](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/37911))\n\n* **command/apply**: Terraform will now raise an explicit error if a plan file intended for one workspace is applied against another workspace. This prevents accidental state corruption when switching between workspaces. The error message clearly indicates the source workspace of the plan and the target workspace. ([#37954](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/37954))\n\n* **command/state show**: The `state show` command will now explicitly fail with exit code 1 when it fails to render the named resources state. Previously, it could exit silently without indicating failure. ([#37933](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/37933))\n\n* **lifecycle**: `replace_triggered_by` now reports an error when given an invalid attribute reference that does not exist in the target resource. This provides clearer feedback to users about configuration mistakes in lifecycle rules. ([#36740](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/36740))\n\n* **backend**: Fixed nil pointer dereference crash during `terraform init` when the destination backend returns an error. The crash occurred when Terraform tried to process error responses from backends without proper null checking. ([#38027](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/38027))\n\n* **testing**: File-level error diagnostics are now included in JUnit XML skipped test elements, ensuring CI/CD pipelines can detect validation failures. This allows test failures that occur during file loading to be properly reported in test result summaries. ([#37801](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/37801))\n\n* **command/plan**: A refresh-only plan could result in a non-zero exit code with no changes, even though a successful refresh should return exit code 0. This has been fixed to properly exit with code 0 when refresh-only plans complete successfully without changes. ([#37406](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/37406))\n\n### Deprecations\n\n* **backend/s3**: Environment variables `AWS_USE_FIPS_ENDPOINT` and `AWS_USE_DUALSTACK_ENDPOINT` now have stricter interpretation. Use the explicit `use_fips_endpoint` and `use_dualstack_endpoint` configuration attributes in the backend block instead of relying on environment variables, or ensure the environment variables are set to exactly `\"true\"` or `\"false\"`. ([#37601](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/37601))\n\n### Experiments\n\nExperiments are only enabled in alpha releases of Terraform CLI. The following features are not yet available in stable releases.\n\n- The experimental \"deferred actions\" feature, enabled by passing the `-allow-deferral` option to `terraform plan`, permits `count` and `for_each` arguments in `module`, `resource`, and `data` blocks to have unknown values and allows providers to react more flexibly to unknown values.\n- `terraform test cleanup`: The experimental `test cleanup` command. In experimental builds of Terraform, a manifest file and state files for each failed cleanup operation during test operations are saved within the `.terraform` local directory. The `test cleanup` command will attempt to clean up the local state files left behind automatically, without requiring manual intervention.\n- `terraform test`: `backend` blocks and `skip_cleanup` attributes:\n  - Test authors can now specify `backend` blocks within `run` blocks in Terraform Test files. Run blocks with `backend` blocks will load state from the specified backend instead of starting from empty state on every execution. This allows test authors to keep long-running test infrastructure alive between test operations, saving time during regular test operations.\n  - Test authors can now specify `skip_cleanup` attributes within test files and within run blocks. The `skip_cleanup` attribute tells `terraform test` not to clean up state files produced by run blocks with this attribute set to true. The state files for affected run blocks will be written to disk within the `.terraform` directory, where they can then be cleaned up manually using the also experimental `terraform test cleanup` command.\n\n## Previous Releases\n\nFor information on prior major and minor releases, refer to their changelogs:\n\n- [v1.14](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/blob/v1.14/CHANGELOG.md)\n- [v1.13](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/blob/v1.13/CHANGELOG.md)\n- [v1.12](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/blob/v1.12/CHANGELOG.md)\n- [v1.11](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/blob/v1.11/CHANGELOG.md)\n- [v1.10](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/blob/v1.10/CHANGELOG.md)\n- [v1.9](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/blob/v1.9/CHANGELOG.md)\n- [v1.8](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/blob/v1.8/CHANGELOG.md)\n- [v1.7](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/blob/v1.7/CHANGELOG.md)\n- [v1.6](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/blob/v1.6/CHANGELOG.md)\n- [v1.5](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/blob/v1.5/CHANGELOG.md)\n- [v1.4](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/blob/v1.4/CHANGELOG.md)\n- [v1.3](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/blob/v1.3/CHANGELOG.md)\n- [v1.2](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/blob/v1.2/CHANGELOG.md)\n- [v1.1](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/blob/v1.1/CHANGELOG.md)\n- [v1.0](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/blob/v1.0/CHANGELOG.md)\n- [v0.15](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/blob/v0.15/CHANGELOG.md)\n- [v0.14](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/blob/v0.14/CHANGELOG.md)\n- [v0.13](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/blob/v0.13/CHANGELOG.md)\n- [v0.12](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/blob/v0.12/CHANGELOG.md)\n- [v0.11 and earlier](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/blob/v0.11/CHANGELOG.md)\n","structuredPatch":[{"oldStart":1,"oldLines":60,"newStart":1,"newLines":63,"lines":[" ## JUnit XML skipped test elements, ensuring CI/CD pipelines can detect validation failures ([#37801](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/37801))\n\n* A refresh-only plan could result in a non-zero exit code with no changes ([#37406](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/37406))\n\n* cli: Fixed crash in `terraform show -json` when plan contains ephemeral resources with preconditions or postconditions ([#37834](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/37834))\n\n* cli: Fixed `terraform init -json` to properly format all backend configuration messages as JSON instead of plain text ([#37911](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/37911))\n\n* `state show`: The `state show` command will now explicitly fail and return code 1 when it fails to render the named resources state ([#37933](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/37933))\n\n* apply: Terraform will raise an explicit error if a plan file intended for one workspace is applied against another workspace ([#37954](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/37954))\n\n* lifecycle: `replace_triggered_by` now reports an error when given an invalid attribute reference that does not exist in the target resource ([#36740](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/36740))\n\n* backend: Fix nil pointer dereference crash during `terraform init` when the destination backend returns an error ([#38027](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/38027))\n\n* stacks: send progress events if the plan fails for better UI integration ([#38039](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/38039))\n\n* cloud: terraform cloud and registry discovery network requests are now more resilient, making temporary network or service related errors less common ([#38064](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/38064))\n\n* stacks: component instances should report no-op plan/apply. This solves a UI inconsistency with convergence destroy plans  ([#38049](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/38049))\n\n\nUPGRADE NOTES:\n\n* backend/s3: The `AWS_USE_FIPS_ENDPOINT` and `AWS_USE_DUALSTACK_ENDPOINT` environment variables now only respect `true` or `false` values, aligning with the AWS SDK for Go. This replaces the previous behavior which treated any non-empty value as `true`. ([#37601](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/37601))\n\n\nEXPERIMENTS:\n\nExperiments are only enabled in alpha releases of Terraform CLI. The following features are not yet available in stable releases.\n\n- The experimental \"deferred actions\" feature, enabled by passing the `-allow-deferral` option to `terraform plan`, permits `count` and `for_each` arguments in `module`, `resource`, and `data` blocks to have unknown values and allows providers to react more flexibly to unknown values.\n- `terraform test cleanup`: The experimental `test cleanup` command. In experimental builds of Terraform, a manifest file and state files for each failed cleanup operation during test operations are saved within the `.terraform` local directory. The `test cleanup` command will attempt to clean up the local state files left behind automatically, without requiring manual intervention.\n- `terraform test`: `backend` blocks and `skip_cleanup` attributes:\n  - Test authors can now specify `backend` blocks within `run` blocks in Terraform Test files. Run blocks with `backend` blocks will load state from the specified backend instead of starting from empty state on every execution. This allows test authors to keep long-running test infrastructure alive between test operations, saving time during regular test operations.\n  - Test authors can now specify `skip_cleanup` attributes within test files and within run blocks. The `skip_cleanup` attribute tells `terraform test` not to clean up state files produced by run blocks with this attribute set to true. The state files for affected run blocks will be written to disk within the `.terraform` directory, where they can then be cleaned up manually using the also experimental `terraform test cleanup` command.\n\n## Previous Releases\n\nFor information on prior major and minor releases, refer to their changelogs:\n\n- [v1.14](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/blob/v1.14/CHANGELOG.md)\n- [v1.13](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/blob/v1.13/CHANGELOG.md)\n- [v1.12](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/blob/v1.12/CHANGELOG.md)\n- [v1.11](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/blob/v1.11/CHANGELOG.md)\n- [v1.10](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/blob/v1.10/CHANGELOG.md)\n- [v1.9](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/blob/v1.9/CHANGELOG.md)\n- [v1.8](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/blob/v1.8/CHANGELOG.md)\n- [v1.7](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/blob/v1.7/CHANGELOG.md)\n- [v1.6](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/blob/v1.6/CHANGELOG.md)\n- [v1.5](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/blob/v1.5/CHANGELOG.md)\n- [v1.4](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/blob/v1.4/CHANGELOG.md)\n- [v1.3](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/blob/v1.3/CHANGELOG.md)\n- [v1.2](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/blob/v1.2/CHANGELOG.md)\n- [v1.1](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/blob/v1.1/CHANGELOG.md)\n- [v1.0](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/blob/v1.0/CHANGELOG.md)\n- [v0.15](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/blob/v0.15/CHANGELOG.md)\n- [v0.14](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/blob/v0.14/CHANGELOG.md)\n- [v0.13](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/blob/v0.13/CHANGELOG.md)\n- [v0.12](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/blob/v0.12/CHANGELOG.md)\n- [v0.11 and earlier](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/blob/v0.11/CHANGELOG.md)\n"}}

This replaces the previous behavior which treated any non-empty value as `true`. Applications that set these variables to any other non-empty string (e.g., `\"yes\"`, `\"1\"`, `\"enabled\"`) will need to change to `\"true\"` or `\"false\"`. ([#37601](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/37601))\n     6→\n     7→### New Features\n     8→\n     9→* **backend/s3**: Support authentication via AWS IAM Identity Center through `aws login`. The S3 backend now integrates with the AWS SDK's credential resolution chain to support AWS IAM Identity Center (SSO) authentication, reducing the need for long-lived access keys. ([#37967](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/37967))\n    10→\n    11→* **variables/outputs**: You can now set a `deprecated` attribute on variable and output blocks to indicate that they are deprecated. This will produce warnings when passing in a value for a deprecated variable or when referencing a deprecated output. Example: `variable \"old_name\" { deprecated = \"Use new_name instead\" }`. ([#38001](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/38001))\n    12→\n    13→* **terraform test**: Test authors can now specify `backend` blocks within `run` blocks in Terraform Test files. Run blocks with `backend` blocks will load state from the specified backend instead of starting from empty state on every execution. This allows test authors to keep long-running test infrastructure alive between test operations, saving time during regular test operations. Backend blocks are only supported in the first apply run block for a given internal state file. ([#34672](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/34672))\n    14→\n    15→* **terraform test**: Test authors can now specify `skip_cleanup` attributes within test files and within run blocks. The `skip_cleanup` attribute tells `terraform test` not to clean up state files produced by run blocks with this attribute set to true. The state files for affected run blocks will be written to disk within the `.terraform` directory, where they can then be cleaned up manually using the also experimental `terraform test cleanup` command. This feature is available in experimental builds of Terraform. ([#34672](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/34672))\n    16→\n    17→* **terraform test**: Allow functions within mock blocks. Test authors can now use Terraform functions like `concat()`, `merge()`, and other built-in functions within mock provider blocks for more dynamic test data generation. ([#34672](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/34672))\n    18→\n    19→* **provisioners**: ssh-based provisioner (file + remote-exec) now re-enables support for PowerShell on Windows targets. This allows Windows users to execute PowerShell scripts via the remote-exec provisioner using the `inline`, `script`, or `scripts` attributes. ([#37794](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/37794))\n    20→\n    21→* **ephemeral resources**: Resource blocks now support `ephemeral` input variables and output values. Ephemeral values are not stored in state and are only computed during the current run, enabling more flexible handling of short-lived data. Ephemeral values can be used with preconditions and postconditions. ([#38001](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/38001))\n    22→\n    23→### Enhancements\n    24→\n    25→* **terraform init**: Log timestamps now include millisecond precision for better timing information in initialization logs. This improves visibility into the duration of init operations and helps diagnose performance issues. ([#37818](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/37818))\n    26→\n    27→* **terraform init**: Skip dependencies declared in development override. When using developer overrides with `terraform init`, Terraform will now skip installing dependencies that are not declared in the override file. This allows you to use `terraform init` with developer overrides without requiring all transitive dependencies to be available. ([#37884](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/37884))\n    28→\n    29→* **lifecycle**: Improved detection of deprecated resource attributes and blocks. The deprecation validation system now provides more accurate error messages when deprecated attributes or blocks are used, helping users migrate to replacement attributes. ([#38077](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/38077))\n    30→\n    31→* **stacks**: Stack runtime now sends progress events if a plan fails, providing better UI integration and real-time feedback during planning operations. ([#38039](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/38039))\n    32→\n    33→* **cloud**: Terraform Cloud and registry discovery network requests are now more resilient, making temporary network or service related errors less common. The implementation includes improved error handling and retry logic for transient failures. ([#38064](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/38064))\n    34→\n    35→* **stacks**: Component instances now correctly report no-op plan and apply operations, solving a UI inconsistency with convergence destroy plans where instances with no changes weren't being displayed properly. ([#38049](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/38049))\n    36→\n    37→### Bug Fixes\n    38→\n    39→* **cli**: Fixed crash in `terraform show -json` when a plan contains ephemeral resources with preconditions or postconditions. The JSON output now correctly serializes ephemeral resource configurations. ([#37834](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/37834))\n    40→\n    41→* **cli**: Fixed `terraform init -json` to properly format all backend configuration messages as JSON instead of mixing plain text with JSON. All diagnostic and informational messages are now consistently JSON-formatted when using the `-json` flag. ([#37911](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/37911))\n    42→\n    43→* **command/apply**: Terraform will now raise an explicit error if a plan file intended for one workspace is applied against another workspace. This prevents accidental state corruption when switching between workspaces. The error message clearly indicates the source workspace of the plan and the target workspace. ([#37954](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/37954))\n    44→\n    45→* **command/state show**: The `state show` command will now explicitly fail with exit code 1 when it fails to render the named resources state. Previously, it could exit silently without indicating failure. ([#37933](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/37933))\n    46→\n    47→* **lifecycle**: `replace_triggered_by` now reports an error when given an invalid attribute reference that does not exist in the target resource. This provides clearer feedback to users about configuration mistakes in lifecycle rules. ([#36740](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/36740))\n    48→\n    49→* **backend**: Fixed nil pointer dereference crash during `terraform init` when the destination backend returns an error. The crash occurred when Terraform tried to process error responses from backends without proper null checking. ([#38049](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/38049))\n\n### Bug Fixes\n\n* **cli**: Fixed crash in `terraform show -json` when a plan contains ephemeral resources with preconditions or postconditions. The JSON output now correctly serializes ephemeral resource configurations. ([#37834](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/37834))\n\n* **cli**: Fixed `terraform init -json` to properly format all backend configuration messages as JSON instead of mixing plain text with JSON. All diagnostic and informational messages are now consistently JSON-formatted when using the `-json` flag. ([#37911](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/37911))\n\n* **command/apply**: Terraform will now raise an explicit error if a plan file intended for one workspace is applied against another workspace. This prevents accidental state corruption when switching between workspaces. The error message clearly indicates the source workspace of the plan and the target workspace. ([#37954](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/37954))\n\n* **command/state show**: The `state show` command will now explicitly fail with exit code 1 when it fails to render the named resources state. Previously, it could exit silently without indicating failure. ([#37933](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/37933))\n\n* **lifecycle**: `replace_triggered_by` now reports an error when given an invalid attribute reference that does not exist in the target resource. This provides clearer feedback to users about configuration mistakes in lifecycle rules. ([#36740](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/36740))\n\n* **backend**: Fixed nil pointer dereference crash during `terraform init` when the destination backend returns an error. The crash occurred when Terraform tried to process error responses from backends without proper null checking.
